        <div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Provincial_Administrative_Divisions_of_Zambia.png" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"></a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia is administratively divided into ten <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Zambia" title="Provinces of Zambia">provinces</a> subdivided into 117 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Zambia" title="Districts of Zambia">districts</a>, and electorally into 156 constituencies and 1,281 wards. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Zambia" title="Human rights in Zambia">Human rights in Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Zambia" title="LGBT rights in Zambia">LGBT rights in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The government is sensitive to the opposition and other criticism and has been quick to prosecute critics using the legal pretext that they had incited <a href="/wiki/Public_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Public disorder">public disorder</a>. <a href="/wiki/Libel_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Libel law">Libel laws</a> are used to suppress free speech and the press.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Same-sex sexual activity is illegal for both males and females in Zambia.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> A 2010 survey revealed that only 2% of Zambians find homosexuality to be morally acceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2019, it was reported that United States Ambassador to Zambia <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lewis_Foote" title="Daniel Lewis Foote">Daniel Lewis Foote</a> was "horrified" by Zambia's jailing of same-sex couple Japhet Chataba and Steven Samba. After an appeal failed and the couple was sentenced to 15 years in prison, Foote asked the Zambian government to review both the case and the country's anti-homosexuality laws. Foote faced a backlash and canceled public appearances after he was threatened on social media, and was subsequently recalled after President Lungu declared him <a href="/wiki/Persona_non_grata" title="Persona non grata">persona non grata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Zambia" title="Geography of Zambia">Geography of Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Zambia" title="Geology of Zambia">Geology of Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/310px-Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/465px-Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/620px-Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Zambia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Zambia map of Köppen climate classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> country in southern Africa, with a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>, and consists mostly of high <a href="/wiki/Plateaus" class="mw-redirect" title="Plateaus">plateaus</a> with some hills and mountains, dissected by river valleys. At 752,614&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (290,586&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) it is the 39th-largest country in the world, slightly smaller than Chile. The country lies mostly between <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a> <a href="/wiki/8th_parallel_south" title="8th parallel south">8°</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_south" title="18th parallel south">18°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/22nd_meridian_east" title="22nd meridian east">22°</a> and <a href="/wiki/34th_meridian_east" title="34th meridian east">34°E</a>. </p>
      <p>Zambia is drained by two major river basins: the <a href="/wiki/Zambezi_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Zambezi River">Zambezi</a>/Kafue basin in the center, west, and south covering about three-quarters of the country; and the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo</a> basin in the north covering about one-quarter of the country. A very small area in the northeast forms part of the internal drainage basin of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Rukwa" title="Lake Rukwa">Lake Rukwa</a> in Tanzania. </p>
      <p>In the Zambezi basin, there are a number of major rivers flowing wholly or partially through Zambia: the <a href="/wiki/Kabompo_River" title="Kabompo River">Kabompo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lungwebungu_River" title="Lungwebungu River">Lungwebungu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kafue_River" title="Kafue River">Kafue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luangwa_River" title="Luangwa River">Luangwa</a>, and the Zambezi itself, which flows through the country in the west and then forms its southern border with <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, Botswana and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>. Its source is in Zambia but it diverts into Angola, and a number of its tributaries rise in Angola's central highlands. The edge of the <a href="/wiki/Cuando_River" title="Cuando River">Cuando River</a> floodplain (not its main channel) forms Zambia's southwestern border, and via the <a href="/wiki/Chobe_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Chobe River">Chobe River</a> that river contributes very little water to the Zambezi because most are lost by evaporation.<sup id="cite_ref-Beilfuss_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beilfuss-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Two of the Zambezi's longest and largest tributaries, the Kafue and the Luangwa, flow mainly in Zambia. Their confluences with the Zambezi are on the border with Zimbabwe at Chirundu and <a href="/wiki/Luangwa,_Zambia" title="Luangwa, Zambia">Luangwa town</a> respectively. Before its confluence, the Luangwa River forms part of Zambia's border with <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>. From Luangwa town, the Zambezi leaves Zambia and flows into Mozambique, and eventually into the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a>. </p>
      <p>The Zambezi falls about 100 metres (328&nbsp;ft) over the 1.6&nbsp;km (0.99&nbsp;mi) wide <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Falls" title="Victoria Falls">Victoria Falls</a>, located in the south-west corner of the country, subsequently flowing into <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kariba" title="Lake Kariba">Lake Kariba</a>. The Zambezi valley, running along the southern border, is both deep and wide. From Lake Kariba going east, it is formed by <a href="/wiki/Graben" title="Graben">grabens</a> and like the Luangwa, Mweru-Luapula, <a href="/wiki/Mweru-wa-Ntipa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mweru-wa-Ntipa">Mweru-wa-Ntipa</a> and Lake Tanganyika valleys, is a <a href="/wiki/Rift_valley" title="Rift valley">rift valley</a>. </p>
      <p>The north of Zambia is very flat with broad plains. In the west the most notable being the <a href="/wiki/Barotse_Floodplain" title="Barotse Floodplain">Barotse Floodplain</a> on the Zambezi, which floods from December to June, lagging behind the annual rainy season (typically November to April). The <a href="/wiki/Floodplain" title="Floodplain">flood</a> dominates the natural environment and the lives, society, and culture of the inhabitants and those of other smaller, floodplains throughout the country. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cataratas_Victoria,_Zambia-Zimbabue,_2018-07-27,_DD_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cataratas_Victoria%2C_Zambia-Zimbabue%2C_2018-07-27%2C_DD_05.jpg/220px-Cataratas_Victoria%2C_Zambia-Zimbabue%2C_2018-07-27%2C_DD_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cataratas_Victoria%2C_Zambia-Zimbabue%2C_2018-07-27%2C_DD_05.jpg/330px-Cataratas_Victoria%2C_Zambia-Zimbabue%2C_2018-07-27%2C_DD_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cataratas_Victoria%2C_Zambia-Zimbabue%2C_2018-07-27%2C_DD_05.jpg/440px-Cataratas_Victoria%2C_Zambia-Zimbabue%2C_2018-07-27%2C_DD_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6819" data-file-height="3891"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cataratas_Victoria,_Zambia-Zimbabue,_2018-07-27,_DD_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Falls" title="Victoria Falls">Victoria Falls</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Eastern Zambia the plateau which extends between the Zambezi and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> valleys is tilted upwards to the north, and so rises imperceptibly from about 900&nbsp;m (2,953&nbsp;ft) in the south to 1,200&nbsp;m (3,937&nbsp;ft) in the centre, reaching 1,800&nbsp;m (5,906&nbsp;ft) in the north near Mbala. These plateau areas of northern Zambia have been categorised by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a> as a large section of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Zambezian_miombo_woodlands" title="Central Zambezian miombo woodlands">Central Zambezian miombo woodlands</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eastern Zambia shows great diversity. The Luangwa Valley splits the plateau in a curve north-east to south-west, extended west into the heart of the plateau by the deep valley of the <a href="/wiki/Lunsemfwa_River" title="Lunsemfwa River">Lunsemfwa River</a>. Hills and mountains are found by the side of some sections of the valley, notably in its north-east the Nyika Plateau (2,200&nbsp;m or 7,218&nbsp;ft) on the Malawi border, which extend into Zambia as the <a href="/wiki/Mafinga_Hills" title="Mafinga Hills">Mafinga Hills</a>, containing the country's highest point, <a href="/wiki/Mafinga_Central" title="Mafinga Central">Mafinga Central</a> (2,339&nbsp;m or 7,674&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Muchinga Mountains, the watershed between the Zambezi and Congo drainage basins, run parallel to the deep valley of the Luangwa River and form a sharp backdrop to its northern edge, although they are almost everywhere below 1,700&nbsp;m (5,577&nbsp;ft). Their culminating peak Mumpu is at the western end and at 1,892&nbsp;m (6,207&nbsp;ft) is the highest point in Zambia away from the eastern border region. The border of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Pedicle" title="Congo Pedicle">Congo Pedicle</a> was drawn around this mountain. </p>
      <p>The southernmost headstream of the Congo River rises in Zambia and flows west through its northern area firstly as the <a href="/wiki/Chambeshi_River" title="Chambeshi River">Chambeshi</a> and then, after the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Bangweulu" title="Lake Bangweulu">Bangweulu Swamps</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Luapula_River" title="Luapula River">Luapula</a>, which forms part of the border with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>. The Luapula flows south then west before it turns north until it enters <a href="/wiki/Lake_Mweru" title="Lake Mweru">Lake Mweru</a>. The lake's other major tributary is the <a href="/wiki/Kalungwishi_River" title="Kalungwishi River">Kalungwishi River</a>, which flows into it from the east. The <a href="/wiki/Luvua_River" title="Luvua River">Luvua River</a> drains Lake Mweru, flowing out of the northern end to the <a href="/wiki/Lualaba_River" title="Lualaba River">Lualaba River</a> (Upper Congo River). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> is the other major <a href="/wiki/Hydrography" title="Hydrography">hydrographic</a> feature that belongs to the Congo basin. Its south-eastern end receives water from the <a href="/wiki/Kalambo_River" title="Kalambo River">Kalambo River</a>, which forms part of Zambia's border with Tanzania. This river has Africa's second highest uninterrupted waterfall, the <a href="/wiki/Kalambo_Falls" title="Kalambo Falls">Kalambo Falls</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Zambia" title="Climate of Zambia">Climate of Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia is located on the plateau of Central Africa, between 1000 and 1600 m above sea level. The average altitude of 1,200 metres (3,900&nbsp;ft) generally has a moderate climate. The climate of Zambia is tropical, modified by elevation. In the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, most of the country is classified as <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wet_and_dry_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical wet and dry climate">tropical wet and dry</a>, with small stretches of semi-arid <a href="/wiki/Steppe_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Steppe climate">steppe climate</a> in the south-west and along the <a href="/wiki/Zambezi_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Zambezi valley">Zambezi valley</a>. </p>
      <p>There are two main seasons, the <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season">rainy season</a> (November to April) corresponding to summer, and the <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> (May/June to October/November), corresponding to winter. The dry season is subdivided into the cool dry season (May/June to August), and the hot dry season (September to October/November). The modifying influence of altitude gives the country pleasant <a href="/wiki/Subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> weather rather than tropical conditions during the cool season of May to August.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> However, average monthly temperatures remain above 20&nbsp;°C (68&nbsp;°F) over most of the country for eight or more months of the year. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:493px;max-width:493px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:119px;max-width:119px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:155px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Rhodesian giraffe" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg/117px-Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg" decoding="async" width="117" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg/176px-Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg/234px-Giraffa_camelopardalis_thornicrofti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4352"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-left">
           <a href="/wiki/Rhodesian_giraffe" title="Rhodesian giraffe">Rhodesian giraffe</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Luangwa_National_Park" title="South Luangwa National Park">South Luangwa National Park</a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:158px;max-width:158px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:155px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg" class="image"><img alt="African fish eagle" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg/156px-African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg" decoding="async" width="156" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg/234px-African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg/312px-African_fish_eagle_just_caught_fish.jpg 2x" data-file-width="672" data-file-height="673"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-left">
           <a href="/wiki/African_fish_eagle" title="African fish eagle">African fish eagle</a>, the national bird of Zambia
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:210px;max-width:210px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:155px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Barbet-zambian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Zambian barbet" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Barbet-zambian.jpg/208px-Barbet-zambian.jpg" decoding="async" width="208" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Barbet-zambian.jpg/312px-Barbet-zambian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Barbet-zambian.jpg/416px-Barbet-zambian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-left">
           <a href="/wiki/Chaplin%27s_barbet" title="Chaplin's barbet">Zambian barbet</a>, Zambia's only true <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> bird species
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are numerous <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> in Zambia, such as forest, thicket, woodland and grassland vegetation types. </p>
      <p>Zambia has approximately 12,505 identified species – 63% animal species, 33% plant species and 4% bacterial species and other microorganisms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There are an estimated 3,543 species of wild flowering plants, consisting of sedges, herbaceous plants and woody plants.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Zambia" title="Northern Province, Zambia">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/North-Western_Province,_Zambia" title="North-Western Province, Zambia">North-Western</a> provinces of the country especially have the highest diversity of flowering plants. Approximately 53% of flowering plants are rare and occur throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A total of <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Zambia" title="List of mammals of Zambia">242 mammal species</a> are found in the country, with most occupying the woodland and grassland ecosystems. The <a href="/wiki/Rhodesian_giraffe" title="Rhodesian giraffe">Rhodesian giraffe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kafue_lechwe" title="Kafue lechwe">Kafue lechwe</a> are some of the well-known subspecies that are <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> to Zambia.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An estimated 757 bird species have been seen in the country, of which 600 are either resident or Afrotropic migrants; 470 breed in the country; and 100 are non-breeding migrants. The <a href="/wiki/Zambian_barbet" class="mw-redirect" title="Zambian barbet">Zambian barbet</a> is a species endemic to Zambia. </p>
      <p>Roughly 490 known fish species, belonging to 24 fish <a href="/wiki/Family_(biology)" title="Family (biology)">families</a>, have been reported in Zambia, with <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> having the highest number of endemic species.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.5/10, ranking it 39th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Zambia" title="Demographics of Zambia">Demographics of Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Zambian_census" title="2010 Zambian census">2010 Zambian census</a>, Zambia's population was 13,092,666. Zambia is racially and ethnically diverse, with 73 distinct ethnic groups. During its occupation by the British between 1911 and 1963, the country attracted immigrants from Europe and the Indian subcontinent, the latter of whom came as indentured workers. While most Europeans left after the collapse of white minority rule, many Asians remained. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg/220px-Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg/330px-Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg/440px-Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="490"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Umutomboko_ceremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Chief <a href="/wiki/Mwata_Kazembe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mwata Kazembe">Mwata Kazembe</a> opens the Mutomboko ceremony
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the first census—conducted on 7 May 1911—there were a total of 1,497 Europeans; 39 Asiatics and an estimated 820,000 Africans. Black Africans were not counted in the six censuses conducted in 1911, 1921, 1931, 1946, 1951, and 1956, prior to independence. By 1956 there were 65,277 Europeans; 5,450 Asiatics; 5,450 Coloureds and an estimated 2,100,000 Africans. </p>
      <p>In the 2010 population census, 99.2% were Black Africans and 0.8% consisted of other racial groups. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style>
      <div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:350px;min-height:150px" data-graph-id="aa1219a1e2a568fdfa618fb4b1d75c017a50bfe1"></div> 
      <p>Zambia is one of the most highly urbanised countries in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> with 44% of the population concentrated along the major transport corridors, while rural areas are sparsely populated. The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 6.2 as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> (6.1 in 1996, 5.9 in 2001–02).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_towns">Largest towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Largest towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Zambia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities and towns in Zambia">List of cities and towns in Zambia</a>
      </div>
      <p>The onset of industrial copper mining on the Copperbelt in the late 1920s triggered rapid urbanisation. Although urbanisation was overestimated during the colonial period, it was substantial.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Mining townships on the Copperbelt soon dwarfed existing centres of population and continued to grow rapidly following Zambian independence. Economic decline on the Copperbelt from the 1970s to the 1990s has altered patterns of urban development but the country's population remains concentrated around the railway and roads running south from the Copperbelt through Kapiri Mposhi, Lusaka, Choma and Livingstone. </p>

         <td style="text-align:right;">1,747,152</td>

           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:orange; width:0.8%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.8%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Not Stated</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:darkblue; width:0.4%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.4%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The population comprises approximately 73 ethnic groups,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> most of which are <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking. Almost 90% of Zambians belong to the nine main ethnolinguistic groups: the <a href="/wiki/Chewa_people" title="Chewa people">Nyanja-Chewa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bemba_people" title="Bemba people">Bemba</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tonga_people_of_Zambia_and_Zimbabwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonga people of Zambia and Zimbabwe">Tonga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tumbuka_people" title="Tumbuka people">Tumbuka</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BaLunda" class="mw-redirect" title="BaLunda">Lunda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lovale_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lovale people">Luvale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kaonde_language" title="Kaonde language">Kaonde</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nkoya" class="mw-redirect" title="Nkoya">Nkoya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lozi_people" title="Lozi people">Lozi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In the rural areas, ethnic groups are concentrated in particular geographic regions. Many groups are small and not well known. However, all the ethnic groups can be found in significant numbers in Lusaka and the Copperbelt. In addition to the linguistic dimension, tribal identities are relevant in Zambia.<sup id="cite_ref-epr_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epr-91">[91]</a></sup> These tribal identities are often linked to family allegiance or to traditional authorities. The tribal identities are nested within the main language groups.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg/500px-Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg" decoding="async" width="500" height="429" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg/750px-Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg/1000px-Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6490" data-file-height="5572"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tribal_Linguistic_map_Zambia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tribal and linguistic map of Zambia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Immigrants, mostly British or South African, as well as some white Zambian citizens of British descent, live mainly in Lusaka and in the Copperbelt in northern Zambia, where they are either employed in mines, financial and related activities or retired. There were 70,000 Europeans in Zambia in 1964, but many have since left the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Zambia_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zambia-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Zambia has a small but economically important Asian population, most of whom are Arabs, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Zambia" title="Indians in Zambia">Indians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Zambia" title="Chinese people in Zambia">Chinese</a>. This minority group has a massive impact on the economy controlling the manufacturing sector. An estimated 80,000 Chinese are resident in Zambia.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In recent years, several hundred dispossessed white farmers have left <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> at the invitation of the Zambian government, to take up farming in the Southern province.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Zambia has a minority of <a href="/wiki/Coloureds" title="Coloureds">coloureds</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed race">mixed race</a>. During colonialism, <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">segregation</a> separated <a href="/wiki/Coloureds" title="Coloureds">coloureds</a>, blacks and whites in public places including schools, hospitals, and in housing. There has been an increase in interracial relationships due to Zambia's growing economy importing labor. Coloureds are not recorded on the census but are considered a minority in Zambia. </p>
      <p>According to the <i>World Refugee Survey 2009</i> published by the <a href="/wiki/US_Committee_for_Refugees_and_Immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants">US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants</a>, Zambia had a population of <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> and asylum seekers numbering approximately 88,900. The majority of refugees in the country came from the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (47,300 refugees from the DRC living in Zambia in 2007), <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> (27,100; see <a href="/wiki/Angolans_in_Zambia" title="Angolans in Zambia">Angolans in Zambia</a>), Zimbabwe (5,400) and Rwanda (4,900).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2009_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2009-96">[96]</a></sup> Zambians are generally welcome to foreigners. </p>
      <p>Beginning in May 2008, the number of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabweans_in_Zambia" title="Zimbabweans in Zambia">Zimbabweans in Zambia</a> began to increase significantly; the influx consisted largely of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabweans_in_South_Africa" title="Zimbabweans in South Africa">Zimbabweans formerly living in South Africa</a> who were fleeing <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia_in_South_Africa#May_2008_riots" title="Xenophobia in South Africa">xenophobic violence there</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IRIN_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-97">[97]</a></sup> Nearly 60,000 refugees live in camps in Zambia, while 50,000 are mixed in with the local populations. Refugees who wish to work in Zambia must apply for permits which can cost up to $500 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2009_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2009-96">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Zambia" title="Religion in Zambia">Religion in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:315px; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">

          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td>

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia is a Christian nation according to the 1996 constitution,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> but a wide variety of religious traditions exist. Traditional religious thoughts blend easily with Christian beliefs in many of the country's <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> churches. About three-fourths of the population is <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> while about 20% follow <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>. Christian denominations include Catholicism, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>, <a href="/wiki/Branhamites" class="mw-redirect" title="Branhamites">Branhamites</a>, and a variety of <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> denominations. </p>
      <p>These grew, adjusted and prospered from the missionary settlements (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and Catholicism in the east from <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>) and Anglicanism (British influences) from the south. Except for some technical positions (e.g. physicians), Western missionary roles have been assumed by native believers. After <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Chiluba" title="Frederick Chiluba">Frederick Chiluba</a> (a Pentecostal Christian) became president in 1991, Pentecostal congregations expanded considerably around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-pentecostal_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentecostal-100">[100]</a></sup> Zambia has one of the largest percentage of <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a> per capita in the world, accounting for about 1 in 18 Zambians.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church_of_Central_Africa" title="Lutheran Church of Central Africa">Lutheran Church of Central Africa</a> has over 11,000 members in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Counting only active preachers, Jehovah's Witnesses in Zambia have over 204,000 adherents<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> with over 930,000 attending their annual observance of Christ's death in 2018. These have been preaching there since 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One in 11 Zambians is a member of the New Apostolic Church.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> With membership above 1,200,000 the Zambia district of the church is the third-largest after Congo East and East Africa (Nairobi).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Followers of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> in Zambia number over 160,000,<sup id="cite_ref-adherents_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adherents-107">[107]</a></sup> or 1.5% of the population. The William Mmutle Masetlha Foundation run by the Baháʼí community is particularly active in areas such as literacy and primary health care. Approximately 1% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Zambia" title="Islam in Zambia">Muslim</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, mostly living in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> There are about 500 people who belong to the <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> sect.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> There is also a small Jewish community, composed mostly of <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazis</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The exact number of Zambian languages is not known although many texts claim that Zambia has 73 languages or 73 languages and dialects. The figure 73 languages is probably due to a non-distinction between language and dialect using the criterion of mutual intelligibility. If this criterion was used, the number of Zambian languages would probably be about 20 or 30 only.<sup id="cite_ref-Chanda,_Vincent_M.,_and,_Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson._2013_1–173_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chanda,_Vincent_M.,_and,_Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson._2013_1–173-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Zambia" title="Languages of Zambia">Languages of Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright" style="">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:fit-content; width:-moz-fit-content; width:-webkit-fit-content;">
        <div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:auto;"> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1017906329">
         <div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:100px;min-height:100px" data-graph-id="074c0dae29c76c7abc1a288a8e48616267b04d86"></div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         Widely spoken languages<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>

         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fdae61; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Nyanja - 14.8
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#abd9e9; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Tonga - 11.4
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#2c7bb6; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Lozi - 5.5
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ffffbf; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Chewa - 4.5
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#abdda4; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;other - 30.3
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The official language of Zambia is English, which is used for official business and instruction in schools. The main local language, especially in Lusaka, is <a href="/wiki/Nyanja" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyanja">Nyanja</a> (Chewa), followed by <a href="/wiki/Bemba_language" title="Bemba language">Bemba</a>. In the Copperbelt <a href="/wiki/Bemba_language" title="Bemba language">Bemba</a> is the main language and <a href="/wiki/Nyanja" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyanja">Nyanja</a> second. <a href="/wiki/Bemba_language" title="Bemba language">Bemba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nyanja" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyanja">Nyanja</a> are spoken in the urban areas in addition to other indigenous languages which are commonly spoken in Zambia. These include <a href="/wiki/Lozi_language" title="Lozi language">Lozi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaonde" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaonde">Kaonde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonga_language_(Zambia_and_Zimbabwe)" title="Tonga language (Zambia and Zimbabwe)">Tonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lunda_languages" title="Lunda languages">Lunda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luvale" class="mw-redirect" title="Luvale">Luvale</a>, which feature on the <a href="/wiki/Zambia_National_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Zambia National Broadcasting Corporation">Zambia National Broadcasting Corporation</a> (ZNBC) local languages section.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chanda,_Vincent_M.,_and,_Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson._2013_1–173_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chanda,_Vincent_M.,_and,_Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson._2013_1–173-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fc8d59; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Chewa_language" title="Chewa language">Chewa</a>
          </div> 
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">

           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fee090; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Lozi_language" title="Lozi language">Lozi</a>
          </div> 
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#e0f3f8; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Lunda_language" title="Lunda language">Lunda</a>
          </div> 
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#91bfdb; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Nyanja_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyanja language">Nyanja</a>
          </div> 
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#4575b4; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Tonga_language_(Zambia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonga language (Zambia)">Tonga</a>
          </div> 
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Urbanisation has had a dramatic effect on some of the indigenous languages, including the assimilation of words from other languages. Urban dwellers sometimes differentiate between urban and rural dialects of the same language by prefixing the rural languages with 'deep'. </p>
      <p>Most will thus speak Bemba and Nyanja in the Copperbelt; Nyanja is dominantly spoken in Lusaka and Eastern Zambia. English is used in official communications and is the language of choice at home among&nbsp;– now common&nbsp;– interethnic families. This evolution of languages has led to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambian_slang&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zambian slang (page does not exist)">Zambian slang</a> heard throughout Lusaka and other major cities. The majority of Zambians usually speak more than one language, the official language, English, and the most spoken language in the town or area they live in. Portuguese has been introduced as a second language into the school curriculum due to the presence of a large Portuguese-speaking Angolan community.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> French is commonly studied in private schools, while some secondary schools have it as an optional subject. A German course has been introduced at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Zambia" title="University of Zambia">University of Zambia</a> (UNZA). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Zambia" title="Education in Zambia">Education in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg/220px-Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg/330px-Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg/440px-Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pupils_at_St_Monicas_Girls_Secondary_School.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Pupils at the St Monica's Girls Secondary School in <a href="/wiki/Chipata" title="Chipata">Chipata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Zambia" title="Eastern Province, Zambia">Eastern Province</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The right to equal and adequate education for all is enshrined within the Zambian constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The Education Act of 2011 regulates equal and quality education.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The Ministry of General Education effectively oversees the provision of quality education through policy and regulation of the education curriculum. </p>
      <p>Fundamentally, the aim of education in Zambia is to promote the full and well-rounded development of the physical, intellectual, social, affective, moral, and spiritual qualities of all learners. The education system has three core structures: <a href="/wiki/Early_childhood_education" title="Early childhood education">Early childhood education</a> and Primary education (Grades 1&nbsp;– 7), Secondary education (Grades 8&nbsp;– 12) and Tertiary education. Adult Literacy programs are available for semi-literate and illiterate individuals. </p>
      <p>The government's annual expenditure on education has increased over the years, increasing from 16.1% in 2006 to 20.2% in 2015. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Zambia" title="Health in Zambia">Health in Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Zambia" title="Healthcare in Zambia">Healthcare in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia is experiencing a generalised <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> epidemic, with a national <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">HIV prevalence rate</a> of 12.40% among adults.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The maternal mortality rate was 398 per 100,000 live births in 2014, compared to 591 in 2007. Over the same period, the under-5 mortality rate dropped to 75 from 119 per 1,000 live births. The prevalence rate of HIV/AIDS for adults aged 15–49 decreased to 13 per cent in 2013/14, from 16 per cent in 2001/02.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Zambia" title="Economy of Zambia">Economy of Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Presently, Zambia averages between $7.5&nbsp;billion and $8&nbsp;billion of exports annually.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> It totalled $9.1&nbsp;billion worth of exports in 2018<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> About 60.5% of Zambians live below the recognised national poverty line,<sup id="cite_ref-mdgs1_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdgs1-122">[122]</a></sup> with rural poverty rates standing at about 77.9%<sup id="cite_ref-mdgs2_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdgs2-123">[123]</a></sup> and urban rates at about 27.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-mdgs3_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdgs3-124">[124]</a></sup> Unemployment and underemployment in urban areas are serious problems. Most rural Zambians are <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence farmers</a>. </p> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">

            <div style="background:#5e4fa2; width:4.2%; overflow: hidden;">

         </tbody>
