       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia ranked 117th out of 128 countries on the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Competitiveness Index">Global Competitiveness Index</a>, which looks at factors that affect economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Social indicators continue to decline, particularly in measurements of life expectancy at birth (about 40.9 years) and maternal mortality (830 per 100,000 pregnancies).<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Zambia fell into poverty after international copper prices declined in the 1970s. The socialist regime made up for falling revenue with several abortive attempts at <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a> programs (SAPs). The policy of not trading through the main supply route and line of rail to the sea&nbsp;– the territory was known as Rhodesia (from 1965 to 1979), and now known as Zimbabwe&nbsp;– cost the economy greatly. After the Kaunda regime, (from 1991) successive governments began limited reforms. The economy stagnated until the late 1990s. In 2007 Zambia recorded its ninth consecutive year of economic growth. Inflation was 8.9%, down from 30% in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Zambia_Export_Treemap_(2014).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Zambia_Export_Treemap_%282014%29.png/220px-Zambia_Export_Treemap_%282014%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Zambia_Export_Treemap_%282014%29.png/330px-Zambia_Export_Treemap_%282014%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Zambia_Export_Treemap_%282014%29.png/440px-Zambia_Export_Treemap_%282014%29.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="520"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Zambia_Export_Treemap_(2014).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Zambia Export Treemap (2014)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia is still dealing with economic reform issues such as the size of the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a>, and improving Zambia's social sector delivery systems.<sup id="cite_ref-dos2009_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos2009-128">[128]</a></sup> Economic regulations and <a href="/wiki/Red_tape" title="Red tape">red tape</a> are extensive, and corruption is widespread. The bureaucratic procedures surrounding the process of obtaining licences encourages the widespread use of facilitation payments.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Zambia's total foreign debt exceeded $6&nbsp;billion when the country qualified for <a href="/wiki/Highly_Indebted_Poor_Country_Initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Highly Indebted Poor Country Initiative">Highly Indebted Poor Country Initiative</a> (HIPC) debt relief in 2000, contingent upon meeting certain <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">performance criteria</a>. Initially, Zambia hoped to reach the HIPC completion point, and benefit from substantial debt forgiveness, in late 2003. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_(current),_%25_of_world_average,_1960-2012;_Zimbabwe,_South_Africa,_Botswana,_Zambia,_Mozambique.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/330px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/495px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/660px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png 2x" data-file-width="1055" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_(current),_%25_of_world_average,_1960-2012;_Zimbabwe,_South_Africa,_Botswana,_Zambia,_Mozambique.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>GDP per capita (current), compared to neighbouring countries (world average = 100)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In January 2003, the Zambian government informed the International Monetary Fund and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> that it wished to renegotiate some of the agreed performance criteria calling for privatisation of the Zambia National Commercial Bank and the national telephone and electricity utilities. Although agreements were reached on these issues, subsequent overspending on civil service wages delayed Zambia's final HIPC debt forgiveness from late 2003 to early 2005, at the earliest. In an effort to reach HIPC completion in 2004, the government drafted an austerity budget for 2004, freezing civil service salaries and increasing the number of taxes. The tax hike and public sector wage freeze prohibited salary increases and new hires. This sparked a nationwide strike in February 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Zambian government is pursuing an economic diversification program to reduce the economy's reliance on the copper industry. This initiative seeks to exploit other components of Zambia's rich resource base by promoting agriculture, tourism, gemstone mining, and hydro-power. In July 2018, Turkish President <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdogan</a> and Zambia's President Edgar Lungu signed 12 agreements in capital Lusaka on areas ranging from trade and investment to tourism and diplomacy.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Zambian economy has historically been based on the <a href="/wiki/Copper_mining" class="mw-redirect" title="Copper mining">copper mining</a> industry. The output of copper had fallen to a low of 228,000 metric tons in 1998 after a 30-year decline in output due to lack of investment, low copper prices, and uncertainty over privatisation. In 2002, following the privatisation of the industry, copper production rebounded to 337,000 metric tons. Improvements in the world copper market have magnified the effect of this volume increase on revenues and foreign exchange earnings. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg/220px-ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg/330px-ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg/440px-ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2224" data-file-height="1698"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ZM-Nkana-headgear-Kitwe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The major Nkana open copper mine, <a href="/wiki/Kitwe" title="Kitwe">Kitwe</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2003, exports of <a href="/wiki/Nonmetal" title="Nonmetal">nonmetals</a> increased by 25% and accounted for 38% of all export earnings, previously 35%. The Zambian government has recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> been granting licenses to international resource companies to prospect for minerals such as nickel, tin, copper, and uranium.<sup id="cite_ref-penny_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-penny-133">[133]</a></sup> The government of Zambia hopes that nickel will take over from copper as the country's top metallic export.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 2009, Zambia was badly hit by the <a href="/wiki/Late_2000s_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Late 2000s recession">world economic crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Agriculture plays a very important part in Zambia's economy providing many more jobs than the mining industry. A small number of <a href="/wiki/White_people_in_Zimbabwe" class="mw-redirect" title="White people in Zimbabwe">white Zimbabwean farmers</a> were welcomed into Zambia after their expulsion by Robert Mugabe, whose numbers had reached roughly 150 to 300 people as of 2004<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> They farm a variety of crops including tobacco, wheat, and chili peppers on an estimated 150 farms. The skills they brought, combined with general economic liberalisation under the late Zambian president <a href="/wiki/Levy_Mwanawasa" title="Levy Mwanawasa">Levy Mwanawasa</a>, has been credited with stimulating an agricultural boom in Zambia. In 2004, for the first time in 26 years, Zambia exported more corn than it imported.<sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel-95">[95]</a></sup> In December 2019, the Zambian government unanimously decided to legalize cannabis for medicinal and export purposes only.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Zambia" title="Tourism in Zambia">Tourism in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg/220px-Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg/330px-Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg/440px-Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Victoriaf%C3%A4lle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Falls" title="Victoria Falls">Victoria Falls</a> (Mosi-oa-Tunya Falls) a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nalikwanda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Nalikwanda.jpg/220px-Nalikwanda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Nalikwanda.jpg/330px-Nalikwanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Nalikwanda.jpg/440px-Nalikwanda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="748" data-file-height="561"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nalikwanda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kuomboka" title="Kuomboka">Kuomboka</a> ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/Lozi_people" title="Lozi people">Lozi people</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia has some of nature's best wildlife and game reserves affording the country with abundant tourism potential. The <a href="/wiki/North_Luangwa_National_Park" title="North Luangwa National Park">North Luangwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Luangwa_National_Park" title="South Luangwa National Park">South Luangwa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kafue_National_Park" title="Kafue National Park">Kafue</a> National Parks have one of the most prolific animal populations in Africa. The Victoria Falls in the Southern part of the country is a major tourist attraction. </p>
      <p>With 73 ethnic groups, there is also a myriad of traditional ceremonies that take place every year. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Zambia" title="List of power stations in Zambia">List of power stations in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2009, Zambia generated 10.3 <a href="/wiki/TWh#Multiples" class="mw-redirect" title="TWh">TWh</a> of electricity and has been rated high in use of both <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">Solar power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">Hydroelectricity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> However, early 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Zambia began experiencing a serious energy shortage due to the poor 2014/2015 rain season, which resulted in low water levels at the Kariba dam and other major dams.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In September 2019, African Green Resources (AGR) announced that it would invest $150&nbsp;million in 50 megawatt (MW) solar farm, along with irrigation dam and expanding the existing grain silo capacity by 80,000 tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nsima_Relishes.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Nsima_Relishes.JPG/220px-Nsima_Relishes.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Nsima_Relishes.JPG/330px-Nsima_Relishes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Nsima_Relishes.JPG/440px-Nsima_Relishes.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="572"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nsima_Relishes.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Nshima" class="mw-redirect" title="Nshima">Nshima</a></i> (top right corner) with three types of <a href="/wiki/Relish" title="Relish">relish</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Prior to the establishment of modern Zambia, the inhabitants lived in independent tribes, each with its own way of life. One of the results of the colonial era was the growth of urbanisation. Different ethnic groups started living together in towns and cities, influencing each other's way of life. They also started adopting aspects of global or universal culture, especially in terms of dressing and mannerisms.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> Much of the original cultures of Zambia have largely survived in rural areas, with some outside influence such as Christianity being widely practiced. Cultures that are specific to certain ethnic groups within Zambia are known as 'Zambian cultures' while those lifestyles that are common across ethnic groups are labelled 'Zambian culture' because they are practiced by almost every Zambian.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> In the urban setting, there is a continuous integration and evolution of these cultures to produce what is called "Zambian culture". </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/170px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/255px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/340px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="2688"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Yombe_people" title="Yombe people">Yombe</a> sculpture, 19th century.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia practices several ceremonies and rituals ranging from nationally recognised traditional ceremonies to unrecognised yet important ceremonies. Many of the ceremonies and rituals are performed on special occasions celebrating or marking achievements, anniversaries, the passage of time, coronations and presidential occasions, atonement and purification, graduation, dedication, oaths of allegiance, initiation, marriage, funeral, birth ceremonies and others.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Like most African countries, Zambia practices both disclosed and undisclosed ceremonies and rituals. Among the disclosed ceremonies and rituals include calendrical or seasonal, contingent, affliction, divination, initiation and regular or daily ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> Undisclosed ceremonies include those practiced in secret such as spiritual groups (e.g. Nyau and Makishi dancers) and traditional marriage counsellors such as alangizi women.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> As of December 2016, Zambia had 77 calendrical or seasonal traditional ceremonies recognized by government and this number will increase in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> These calendrical ceremonies that takes place once per year include Nc’wala, Kulonga, Kuoboka, Malaila, Nsengele, Chibwela kumushi, Dantho, Ntongo, Makundu, Lwiindi, Chuungu, and Lyenya. These known as <a href="/wiki/Zambian_traditional_ceremonies" title="Zambian traditional ceremonies">Zambian traditional ceremonies</a>. Some of the more prominent are: <a href="/wiki/Kuomboka" title="Kuomboka">Kuomboka</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kathanga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kathanga (page does not exist)">Kathanga</a> (Western Province), <a href="/wiki/Kazembe#Mutomboko_Festival" title="Kazembe">Mutomboko</a> (Luapula Province), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kulamba_ceremony&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kulamba ceremony (page does not exist)">Kulamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ncwala" class="mw-redirect" title="Ncwala">Ncwala</a> (Eastern Province), <a href="/wiki/Lwiindi" title="Lwiindi">Lwiindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shimunenga" title="Shimunenga">Shimunenga</a> (Southern Province), <a href="/wiki/Lunda_Lubanza" title="Lunda Lubanza">Lunda Lubanza</a> (North Western), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Likumbi_Lyamize&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Likumbi Lyamize (page does not exist)">Likumbi Lyamize</a> (North Western),<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_Lukwakwa" title="Mbunda Lukwakwa">Mbunda Lukwakwa</a> (North Western Province), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chibwela_Kumushi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chibwela Kumushi (page does not exist)">Chibwela Kumushi</a> (Central Province), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vinkhakanimba&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vinkhakanimba (page does not exist)">Vinkhakanimba</a> (Muchinga Province), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ukusefya_Pa_Ng%27wena&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ukusefya Pa Ng'wena (page does not exist)">Ukusefya Pa Ng'wena</a> (Northern Province). </p>
      <p>Popular traditional arts include pottery, basketry (such as <a href="/wiki/Tonga_baskets" title="Tonga baskets">Tonga baskets</a>), stools, fabrics, mats, wooden carvings, ivory carvings, wire craft, and copper crafts. Most <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Zambia" title="Music of Zambia">Zambian traditional music</a> is based on drums (and other percussion instruments) with a lot of singing and dancing. In urban areas, foreign genres of music are popular, particularly Congolese <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">rumba</a>, African-American music and Jamaican reggae. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Zambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Media in Zambia">Media in Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Zambia" title="Telecommunications in Zambia">Telecommunications in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Ministry of Information and Broadcasting Services in Zambia is responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Zambian_News_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Zambian News Agency">Zambian News Agency</a>, while there are also numerous media outlets throughout the country which include; television stations, newspapers, <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM radio stations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Online_journalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Online journalism">Internet news websites</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_Games">Sports and Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Sports and Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Sports and games are common social aspects of Zambian culture(s) that brings people together for learning, development of skills, fun and joyous moments.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> Sports and games in Zambia include but not limited to football, athletics, netball, volleyball and indigenous games such as nsolo, chiyenga, waida, hide and seek, walyako, and sojo.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> These are some of the indigenous games that support socialisation. All these sports and games are part of the Zambian culture(s). The fact that the games are played by more than one person makes them social and edutainment events.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> The history of some of these games is as old as Zambians themselves. However, Zambia started taking part in popular global sports and games mainly in 1964 Summer olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206_142-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mkandawire,_Sitwe_Benson.,_Simooya,_Steriah_Monica.,_and_Monde,_Pauline_Namakau._2019_1–206-142">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Zambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport in Zambia">Sport in Zambia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg/220px-Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg/330px-Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg/440px-Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Inauguration_of_Edgar_Lungu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_Heroes_Stadium" title="National Heroes Stadium">National Heroes Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lusaka" title="Lusaka">Lusaka</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Zambia declared its independence on the day of the closing ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/1964_Summer_Olympics" title="1964 Summer Olympics">1964 Summer Olympics</a>, thereby becoming the first country ever to have entered an Olympic game as one country, and leave it as another. In 2016, Zambia participated for the thirteenth time in the Olympic games. Two medals were won. The medals were won successively in boxing and on the track. In 1984 Keith Mwila won a bronze medal in the light flyweight. In 1996 Samuel Matete won a silver medal in the 400-metre hurdles. Zambia has never participated in the Winter Olympics. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Zambia, and the <a href="/wiki/Zambia_national_football_team" title="Zambia national football team">Zambia national football team</a> has had its triumphant moments in football history. At the <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Seoul Olympics">Seoul Olympics</a> in 1988, the national team defeated the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italian national team</a> with a score of 4–0. <a href="/wiki/Kalusha_Bwalya" title="Kalusha Bwalya">Kalusha Bwalya</a>, Zambia's most celebrated football player, and one of Africa's greatest football players in history scored a hat trick in that match. However, to this day, many pundits say the greatest team Zambia has ever assembled was the one that perished on 28 April 1993 in a <a href="/wiki/1993_Zambia_national_football_team_air_disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="1993 Zambia national football team air disaster">plane crash</a> at <a href="/wiki/Libreville,_Gabon" class="mw-redirect" title="Libreville, Gabon">Libreville, Gabon</a>. Despite this, in 1996, Zambia was ranked 15th on the official FIFA World Football Team rankings, the highest attained by any southern African team. In 2012, Zambia won the <a href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="African Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> for the first time after losing in the final twice. They beat Côte d'Ivoire 8–7 in a penalty shoot-out in the final, which was played in Libreville, just a few kilometers away from the plane crash 19 years previously.<sup id="cite_ref-Africa_Cup_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Africa_Cup-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Union">Rugby Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> are also popular sports in Zambia. Notably, at one point in the early 2000s, the <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Australia national rugby union team">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_union_team" title="South Africa national rugby union team">South Africa</a> national rugby teams were captained by players born in the same <a href="/wiki/Lusaka" title="Lusaka">Lusaka</a> hospital, <a href="/wiki/George_Gregan" title="George Gregan">George Gregan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corn%C3%A9_Krige" title="Corné Krige">Corné Krige</a>. Zambia boasts having the highest rugby poles in the world, located at Luanshya Sports Complex in <a href="/wiki/Luanshya" title="Luanshya">Luanshya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Zambia" title="Rugby union in Zambia">Rugby union in Zambia</a> is a minor but growing sport. They are currently ranked 73rd by the <a href="/wiki/International_Rugby_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="International Rugby Board">IRB</a> and have 3,650 registered players and three <i>formally organised</i> clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-IRB_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRB-146">[146]</a></sup> Zambia used to play cricket as part of <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>. Zambia has also strangely provided a <a href="/wiki/Shinty" title="Shinty">shinty</a> international, Zambian-born <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Tembo" title="Eddie Tembo">Eddie Tembo</a> representing Scotland in the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_rules_Shinty/Hurling" class="mw-redirect" title="Compromise rules Shinty/Hurling">compromise rules Shinty/Hurling</a> game against <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Ireland</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, Zambia was due to host the <a href="/wiki/2011_All-Africa_Games" title="2011 All-Africa Games">tenth All-Africa Games</a>, for which three stadiums were to be built in <a href="/wiki/Lusaka" title="Lusaka">Lusaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ndola" title="Ndola">Ndola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Livingstone,_Zambia" title="Livingstone, Zambia">Livingstone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-games_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-games-148">[148]</a></sup> The Lusaka stadium would have a capacity of 70,000 spectators while the other two stadiums would hold 50,000 people each. The government was encouraging the private sector to get involved in the construction of the sports facilities because of a shortage of public funds for the project. Zambia later withdrew its bid to host the 2011 All-Africa Games, citing a lack of funds. Hence, Mozambique took Zambia's place as host. </p>
      <p>Zambia also produced the first black African (<a href="/wiki/Madalitso_Muthiya" title="Madalitso Muthiya">Madalitso Muthiya</a>) to play in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Golf_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Golf Open">United States Golf Open</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> one of the four major golf tournaments. </p>
      <p>In 1989, the country's <a href="/wiki/Zambia_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Zambia national basketball team">basketball team</a> had its best performance when it qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA Africa Championship">FIBA Africa Championship</a> and thus finished as one of Africa's top ten teams.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Zambia hosted and won the Pan-African football tournament <a href="/wiki/2017_Africa_U-20_Cup_of_Nations" title="2017 Africa U-20 Cup of Nations">U-20 African Cup of Nation</a> for players age 20 and under.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Zambia's culture has been an integral part of their development post-independence such as the uprising of cultural villages and private museums. The music which introduced dance is part of their cultural expression and it embodies the beauty and spectacle of life in Zambia, from the intricacies of the talking drums to the <i>Kamangu</i> drum used to announce the beginning of <i>Malaila</i> traditional ceremony. Dance as a practice serves as a unifying factor bringing the people together as one.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zamrock">Zamrock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Zamrock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Zamrock" title="Zamrock">Zamrock</a> is a musical genre that emerged in the 1970s, and has developed a cult following in the West. Zamrock has been described as mixing traditional Zambian music with heavy repetitive riffs similar to groups such as <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">Rolling Stones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-154">[154]</a></sup> Notable groups in the genre include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rikki_Ililonga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rikki Ililonga (page does not exist)">Rikki Ililonga</a> and his band <a href="/w/index.php?title=Musi-O-Tunya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Musi-O-Tunya (page does not exist)">Musi-O-Tunya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witch_(Zamrock_band)" title="Witch (Zamrock band)">WITCH</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chrissy_%22Zebby%22_Tembo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chrissy &quot;Zebby&quot; Tembo (page does not exist)">Chrissy "Zebby" Tembo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ngozi" title="Paul Ngozi">Paul Ngozi</a> and his Ngozi Family.<sup id="cite_ref-azambianband_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azambianband-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-156">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Zambia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
